Central Government and National Government Hold Separate

Commemoration of the Founding of the Revolutionary Government

Sun Ke Reports on the Difficult Struggles of the Premier

Chairman Lin Speaks About Recalling the Revolutionary Spirit of the Premier

(Nanjing) The 5th is the twelfth anniversary of the founding of the Revolutionary Government. All government agencies, groups, and schools in the capital are given a day off. Newspapers are also suspended for a day. The entire city flies flags to celebrate. The Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and all sectors of the capital held commemorative meetings separately in the morning. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Nanjing) The Central Government held a commemoration meeting for the founding of the Revolutionary Government at 8:00 a.m. on the 5th. Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Sun Ke, Dai Chuanxian, Shi Ying, Chen Lifu, Huang Musong, Ma Chaojun, Zheng Zhannan, Dai Kuisheng, Xie Zuomin, Gu Zhenggang, Miao Peicheng, Deng Jiayan, and others, as well as all staff members and representatives of various agencies, totaling approximately 600 people, attended. The meeting began with music, chaired by Sun Ke, who led the ceremony. Sun Ke gave a speech, the original text of which is as follows: Fellow comrades, today is the twelfth anniversary of the founding of the Revolutionary Government. To commemorate the day when the Premier took office as the Extraordinary President in Guangzhou, we cannot but recall the history of the Revolutionary Government's struggle in Guangzhou from 1921 to 1924. In 1921, the Northern Warlords Cao and Wu were in power, holding the Chinese government and destroying the revolutionary forces. In order to carry out the revolutionary purpose, the Premier returned to Guangzhou from Shanghai. At that time, some congressmen followed the Premier back to Guangzhou. After the Premier returned to Guangzhou, in order to establish a revolutionary central force to maintain the revolutionary movement with the formal highest authority for internal and external affairs, he advocated the speedy establishment of the Revolutionary Government. At that time, Chen Jiongming was in charge of Guangdong Province, but Chen Jiongming had colluded with Cao and Wu and secretly opposed the establishment of the Revolutionary Government in Guangzhou. Although Chen Jiongming opposed it in this way, in order to carry out his revolutionary advocacy, the Premier held the ceremony of taking office as the Extraordinary President on May 5, 1921. We still remember that on the day the Revolutionary Government was founded, hundreds of thousands of people in Guangzhou participated in a grand parade and enthusiastically expressed their approval. After the establishment of the Revolutionary Government, the Premier actively prepared to send troops north. At that time, Chen Jiongming secretly undermined the revolutionary movement in Guangdong. Therefore, in the autumn of that year, the Premier led a part of the army and comrades from other provinces to Guilin, Guangxi, as the base camp to prepare to send troops to Hunan. Later, the Premier learned that the internal situation in Guangdong was unstable and was deeply afraid that Chen Jiongming would surrender to the Northern Warlords. Therefore, he decided to withdraw his troops from Guilin to Guangzhou to suppress the rebellion. In 1922, the Premier returned to Guangzhou to prepare to send troops from Guangdong to Jiangxi. At that time, Chen Jiongming expressed his obedience on the surface, but in fact, he was actively resisting. Therefore, Chen Jiongming himself expressed his resignation and removed himself from his various positions before the Premier returned and left Guangzhou, indicating that he would not participate in the Northern Expedition movement. After Chen Jiongming left the Premier, he continued to actively resist secretly. On June 16 of that year, he rebelled in Guangzhou, causing the Premier to suffer misfortune. In August of 1922, the Premier returned to Shanghai and ordered the various armies in Guangxi to move east to expel the rebel Chen. In the winter of 1922, when the army was launched from the West River, it defeated the rebel army. In 1923, the Premier returned to Guangdong again, reorganized the base camp, and continued the task of the Northern Expedition. The position of the Revolutionary Government in Guangdong from 1923 to 1924 was the most difficult, because at that time, the revolutionary forces only reached Guangzhou, Chen rebel occupied the East River, and the other Northern Jiangxi was not subject to the orders of the Revolutionary Government. At that time, the revolutionary forces could only rely on a corner of Guangzhou to maintain. At the same time, because the Revolutionary Government wanted to resist the Northern Warlords and withhold Guangdong customs duties, it aroused the resistance of the imperialists. The United Kingdom assisted the Northern Warlords in negotiating with the Revolutionary Government and sent warships to intimidate them. At the same time, it colluded with the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce to create a reactionary force to overthrow the Revolutionary Government. At that time, the Revolutionary Government in Guangzhou had to go through a very difficult struggle to eliminate all kinds of reactionary labor forces. After the Premier went north, the reactionary forces in Guangdong gradually disappeared. When we recall this history of difficult struggle in the years after the establishment of the Revolutionary Government, it is more difficult than the position of our party and country today. We must inherit the Premier's great spirit and strive forward. Since the September 18th Incident, our comrades have often become pessimistic because they have been subjected to this kind of aggression and oppression by Japanese imperialism, and because the country cannot unite and often has external failures, thinking that the party and country have no way out and that the future seems very dark. The brothers believe that the environment we are in now is certainly difficult, but the difficulty at this time is not as difficult as when the Premier was in Guangzhou. Now the political power in the country is still in the hands of our party. We already have various forces such as politics and military affairs. We cannot say that there are too many difficulties and we cannot break through the situation. As long as we can restore the great spirit of the Premier in establishing the Revolutionary Government in Guangzhou and organizing the revolutionary movement and carry it forward, all difficulties can be broken. Therefore, today we commemorate the establishment of the Revolutionary Government, we must restore the Premier's revolutionary spirit, consolidate the revolutionary forces, concentrate the revolutionary forces of the national people, resist the aggression of the imperialists externally, and eliminate all the evil forces that destroy the revolutionary front internally, so that the country and the nation can continue to survive, and the revolutionary mission can be completed in accordance with the Premier's legacy. This is the important responsibility that all of our comrades should have the determination to shoulder today in commemorating the Premier's establishment of the Revolutionary Government in Guangzhou. (Central News Agency, 5th)

(Nanjing) The National Government held a commemoration meeting for the founding of the Revolutionary Government at 5:00 a.m. on the 5th. Chairman Lin and the heads of various departments and committees, civil officials, and military counselors attended the meeting. Chairman Lin led the ceremony and gave a report entitled "Recalling the Revolutionary Spirit of the Premier to Save the Current National Crisis." The original text is as follows: Everyone, today is the anniversary of the founding of the Revolutionary Government. This anniversary is the day when the Premier took office as the Extraordinary President in Guangzhou. Originally, the Premier was completely responsible for the revolutionary cause. For decades, he ran around without leisure and suffered hardships. He was only responsible for the Republic of China and had no thought of rights. We remember that the Premier first took office as the Provisional President on January 1, the first year of the Republic of China, after the Wuchang Uprising was completed. When the Premier returned from overseas and arrived in Shanghai, the first issue he discussed with his comrades was to build the Republic of China. First, we must unify China. To unify China, we must first start with the organization of the Presidential Palace. At that time, many people did not understand this meaning. I remember that during the discussion of the presidential issue, someone proposed the system of Grand Marshal and Deputy Marshal. They thought that although the Wuchang Uprising was said to be successful, it had not yet reached the north, and it was still in the name of Grand Marshal and Deputy Marshal to lead the situation. Their advocacy completely did not understand the Premier's meaning. They did not know that the Premier really had a lot of hard work at that time. Later, after Mr. Chen Yingshi explained to the general comrades, the proposal to abandon the Grand Marshal and Deputy Marshal was finally approved, and the name Provisional President was used. In this way, we know the Premier's spirit of advancing bravely in the revolution throughout his life. Even if there are mistakes, they are all due to the comrades' incomprehension, and this is the twist when the Premier first served as Provisional President. On May 5, the tenth year of the Republic of China, when he served as Extraordinary President in Guangzhou, there was also a very solemn discussion beforehand, but there were also some people who did not understand the Premier's meaning and obstructed it. Now we remember that there are a few words in the Premier's legacy, saying that people should aim to do great things, not to be high officials. What is this great thing? In simple terms, it is the National Revolution, which is to demand the independence, freedom, and equality of China. People who do not understand the Premier's meaning think that the Premier has already served as the Provisional President and has already ceded to Yuan Shikai, so under the banner of protecting the law, it is better to use the name of Grand Marshal to organize the Grand Marshal's Office and the Base Camp. They thought that this would allow them to continue and support the precarious situation. They only knew that Guangzhou was the birthplace of the revolution, but they did not know that it must be developed and expanded from the birthplace before it could unify China. The Premier's work of the Northern Expedition was to unify China. If China is not unified, it will always be a precarious situation no matter what. At the same time, some people advocated the theory of inter-provincial autonomy, but it was not a solution. Therefore, before May 5, the tenth year of the Republic of China, the issue of the presidency was discussed in Guangzhou for almost more than a month, and there were still many people who came out to obstruct it, advocating to stay in a precarious situation and not develop outwards. The Premier had to struggle in such a difficult environment, and had to bravely come forward and take the post of Extraordinary President. This expression of spirit is to be responsible for the Northern Expedition, to complete the unification, and to enable China to embark on the road of independence, freedom, and equality. However, in the end, because some people were not devoted to the Premier's beliefs and did not implement them effectively, they hindered many workers and did not urge the Premier forward in a unified manner. This is really regrettable. The Premier devoted his life to the revolution, day after day for decades, but he rarely received the assistance of the majority of the people, so that the Three People's Principles have not been realized today, because everyone does not pay attention to carefully studying, and there is a suspicion, such as the protection of the law, the general senators in Beiping all arrived in Guangzhou to hold a meeting, and then organized a constitutional drafting meeting, after several months of discussion, the constitution will be completed, suddenly someone came out to destroy, thinking that once the constitution is completed, Guangzhou will become a formal situation, so they do not hesitate to engage in destruction by cruel means. These people who destroy are also knowledgeable and capable people, only because they do not have a long-term vision, they see their own interests, they do not see the interests of the country, they are content and lucky, they try to survive, they delay the country, to this day. Today, we are holding this meeting, recalling that the Premier was so responsible to the country, so struggling for the revolution, and so painstakingly explaining to comrades and the people who do not understand. Today, some of our armed comrades are fighting desperately with the enemy on the front line, and some are making great sacrifices in suppressing bandits. Our comrades in the rear should bravely move forward with the Premier's fearless spirit, break through difficulties, stand on a battle line with the armed comrades on the front line, and fight to the end, so that the national crisis can be resolved. (Central News Agency, 5th)

Suspicious Case of Japanese Military Officer

A Large Number of Valuable Jewelry Found on His Person

Why Did Shiga Commit Suicide?

Nona's Biography

The President of Hunan Political Science University, Luo Jie, once wrote a biography of Nona, describing his revolutionary experiences and miraculous deeds as follows: He is called the Three Hutuktu and the Seventh Hobilghan, named Chengli Jiamucuo, now a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, Nona Hutuktu. Tibetan soldiers regard him as a divine person, and the people of Xikang admire him as a pioneer of the revolution. Hobilghan means reincarnation. Nona entered Beijing in the nineteenth year of the Republic of China to receive orders. During his spare time discussing Kang affairs, he spread the Dharma and healed diseases, attracting a large number of people. He did not claim any supernatural powers, but single-mindedly focused on matters of principle, encouraging his disciples to endure hardship and uphold precepts as the foundation. People in the capital all praised him, vying to meet him. In Tibetan Buddhism, the Exoteric Buddhism was founded in ancient times, known as Po Mu. At the end of the Zhou Dynasty, the Xueshan Temple was built. Esoteric Buddhism was founded in the Eastern Jin Dynasty. Five Indian masters, especially Hua Sheng Dashi, greatly prospered it. The great ten reincarnations faced dangers and difficulties in successive lifetimes, spreading compassion widely. The five divisions of Buddha, Golden Lotus, and Vajra were able to be greatly promoted and have not declined to this day. Tibetan people are known for their bravery and skill in battle. Gradually, they learned the teachings of compassion, forbearance, and humility, mostly worshiping Buddhism, cherishing peace and tranquility, which gradually became their custom. Tibet is largest in the Front and Back Tibet, followed by Xikang. Xikang is centered in Batang. The eastern regions of Batang, where thirty-three counties were established during the Qing Dynasty, still retain the old system of Tusi. In the Batang area, the four Hutuktus still concurrently manage politics and religion. The four Hutuktus are Basu, Chaya, Qamdo, and Leiwuqi, with Leiwuqi being the largest. Its territory borders the twenty-five tribes of Qinghai to the north, and the central part of Baimagang to the south. Qamdo is the middle arm, Danda Mountain is the left arm, and Basu and Chaya are located in the southeast, with the thirty-nine tribes shielding the northwest. It is truly a sacred land of the Red Sect. During the Yuan and Ming dynasties, they were conferred the title of Nomunhan. During the reign of Emperor Kangxi of the Qing Dynasty, the title was changed to Grand Hutuktu. During the fifty-eighth year of Emperor Qianlong's reign, Sangji Yiji, a monk official of the Nona Temple, assisted General Fukang'an in conquering the Gurkhas, and was conferred the title of Three Hutuktu. The direct transmission of Hua Sheng's ancestor, called Meier Dana, was actually Nona's original teacher. Meier Dana did not concern himself with political affairs, but focused on the three divisions of Esoteric Buddhism, Buddha, Golden Lotus, and Vajra, comprehensively mastering and harmonizing them, compassionately saving sentient beings, and repeatedly demonstrating supernatural transformations. He lived to be over 130 years old, and then passed away after achieving enlightenment. Nona was born in Xiaji in the ugly hour of the fifteenth day of the fifth month of the lunar calendar in the fourth year of Tongzhi of the Qing Dynasty (Yi Chou). Because he was a Hobilghan, he was welcomed into the temple at the age of seven. He fully inherited his teacher's essence, possessing profound knowledge of both Exoteric and Esoteric Buddhism, and devoted himself to compassion. At the age of twenty-five, he took over the administration of Leiwuqi. Twelve years later, he and his younger brother went to pay homage to Gongduo Bazhang Mountain in Baimagang. The wild tribes were fierce and cruel, and his brother was killed. The Grand Hutuktu was furious and led Nona to conquer the wild tribes, expanding the territory of Baima, implementing both political and religious governance. After seven years, a rough framework was established, which was presented to the central dynasty. In the first year of the Republic of China, he returned to Leiwuqi with a tin staff. The following year, the Tibetan army invaded Kang, and the Sichuan governor ordered generals to send troops to conquer. Nona and the Grand Hutuktu led troops to assist in the battle, recovering the invaded lands of the thirty-nine tribes and the twenty-five tribes. He had been at odds with the Dalai Lama for seven years. When the Tibetan army launched a full-scale attack, Nona, seeing that Qamdo was surrounded by mountains on all sides and the city was like being at the bottom of a well, worried that if the mountains were occupied by the enemy, they would be trapped and waiting to be captured. He requested that the army led by Peng Risheng move troops to firmly defend the mountain passes and await reinforcements, but his advice was not heeded. Soon, the mountains were all occupied by the enemy. He advised breaking through and retreating to Qinghai, but again his advice was not heeded. Risheng then surrendered his army. Liu, the battalion commander of the Han camp, fought valiantly but was defeated and drowned in the river. Hundreds of soldiers followed him in death. Nona was defeated and captured. The Dalai Lama ordered him to surrender, but he refused. The Dalai Lama then dug a deep pit outside Lhasa, about several feet deep, piled up wood and stone, and covered it with several thatched roofs. Three hundred soldiers were stationed there, leaving a hole only five inches wide. Food and water were lowered once a day. At first, they tried to induce him to surrender, but after a long time, they realized he would not yield. They placed the food on the ground for him. Nona groped for food in the dark cell and eventually died. After several days, he revived. The guards tried to test him by lowering a bundle of straws. Nona groped for the food, and the guards considered him a divine person and no longer placed the food on the ground. Nona fought six battles in the prison, reciting the Buddha's name all day long, focusing his mind on one state. After his daily tasks, he dug the earth with his hands. When he encountered a stone, he changed direction and dug again. After a long time, he created a hole and escaped, seeing the light of day again. Then, he traveled secretly at night, taking the path to India, traversing rugged ridges, begging for food to survive. Whenever he encountered illness, he treated it. Passing through Zhaxi Kong, he cured the daughter of a prince, who had been haunted by demons for a long time, with a curse. The prince, grateful, kept him in the temple. Nona, longing for the interior, devised a plan to send his followers east. Passing through Mumbai, Baloch, and other places, he reached the interior after nine months of hardship. When he was imprisoned in the earthen cell, it was damp, filthy, and the food was meager. Swarms of insects bit him, enough to weaken and kill him. However, Nona survived for six years, returning to life after death, and even used his flesh and blood to replace tools, breaking through solid and thick barriers. The guards had no awareness at all, which was an especially incredible feat. Ding Zipei, a representative of Xikang, said that in the past, the Tibetans worshiped Nona's corpse and built a pagoda, calling him the Holy Emperor. The Dalai Lama thought he was certainly dead. After several years, they suddenly heard that he was still alive. He sent people to secretly seek Nona's portrait, and upon careful examination, it was indeed him. He then beat to death one of the guards. When Nona escaped from the difficult situation, he must have faked his death to show his passing. If it were not for his sincere faith and conduct moving the Buddhas to add their power, how could he have achieved this? I once raised this question to Nona, but he remained silent, perhaps avoiding speaking of supernatural powers. Earlier, Yin Changheng, the governor of Sichuan, ordered General Liu Ruilin to garrison Kang. Ruilin had the courage to resist strong enemies. Former President Yuan Shikai withdrew Changheng back to Sichuan, and Ruilin was dismissed along with him, replaced by Peng Risheng as general. That was in the third year of the Republic of China. Risheng was cowardly and lacked courage. The lands of the thirty-nine tribes were lost due to his inability to defend them. More than half of the Leiwuqi soldiers were killed or injured. For more than a year, they were burdened with extortion and providing for teachers, and aid was cut off. The following year, Shikai and the governor of Sichuan sent troops to Leiwuqi, ordering Nona to go to Lhasa to negotiate the withdrawal of troops. Before the negotiations were completed, Peng's army started a war over a minor matter. The central government was in turmoil, and reinforcements did not arrive. The exhausted and isolated army resisted the enemy for two years, and the territory of Leiwuqi was completely lost. The Grand Hutuktu was captured after exhausting his strength and poisoned to death in Lhasa. Peng Chu, the leader of the thirty-nine tribes, was captured and had his nose cut off. The Second Hutuktu died of fright because the Dalai Lama blamed him for helping the Han people. Nona led more than 700 monks, laypeople, and remnants of the army to retreat to Qamdo with Peng's army, begging for help from Chen Xialing, the garrison commander of Qamdo. Xialing did not respond. All of this was the cause of the defeat in Xikang. In the winter of the thirteenth year, he arrived in Beijing and visited the President of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, but was rejected. He visited the ruling Duan, but the gatekeepers would not let him pass. Nona was filled with grief and indignation, intending to commit suicide by smashing his head in sacrifice for Kang. The soldiers were surprised and stopped him from saving him. He then reached the ruling Duan. The ruling Duan treated him with respect and learned Buddhism from him, promising to send him back to Kang and restore his old possessions. When the ruling Duan stepped down, Liu Fucheng, the Sichuan army border defense governor of the Northern Expedition of the party army, heard of Nona's virtue and respectfully welcomed him into the army, spreading Esoteric Buddhism. More than ten thousand disciples were taught by him. Nona never boasted about himself. His knowledge and ability far surpassed others. People in Beijing who were concerned about Kang affairs heard that Nona was skilled in politics and knew military affairs, disciplined himself with integrity, sacrificed everything, and wholeheartedly sought unity. At first, they thought he was an ordinary person. Later, they learned that he was the reincarnated living Buddha of the seventh generation, and they longed to see him.

Miao Zhongxiu Goes to the United States to Investigate Silk Industry

Jiangzhe Silk Industry Groups Fete Him Yesterday

The General Office of Jiangzhe-Anhui Silk Cocoons and the Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association believe that the United States is the largest consumer of raw silk in the world, importing 550,000 dan of raw silk annually, of which 90% is purchased from Japan. China and Italy, etc., only supply one-tenth. In recent years, the Chinese government and business community have been striving to remedy this situation, and have successively established the Old Silk Sorting Association and Promotion Association. Recently, they have organized the United Sericulture Control Association to unify silkworm breeds and increase cocoon production. However, there is little connection with foreign markets. The Japanese government recently established a Raw Silk Visiting Bureau in New York to vigorously promote Japanese silk sales in the United States, and has also made false propaganda about the Chinese silk industry. The chairman of the General Office and Trade Association, Zhu Jing'an and Shen Huachen, requested Miao Zhongxiu, director of the Raw Silk Inspection Department of the Commodity Inspection Bureau, to go to the United States for practical liaison to promote sales. This plan was sponsored by the Old Silk Promotion Committee and the Commodity Inspection Bureau, and approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Mr. Miao is scheduled to sail on the President Cleveland on the 9th of this month. Yesterday, the General Office of Jiangzhe-Anhui Silk Cocoons, the Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association, and the Jiangzhe Old Silk Promotion Committee specially held a banquet at the Xinya Restaurant on Nanjing Road to see him off. It is reported that in addition to carrying out the above tasks, Mr. Miao also intends to investigate the status of the Japanese and American raw silk inspection offices for reference. After completing his work in the United States, he will return to China via Europe. After arriving in France, he plans to go to Lyon to investigate the silk industry.

Suggests Establishing a Respect Agriculture Day

To Commemorate the Birth of Shennong

The Shanghai South District Farmers Association convened village leaders yesterday to hold a memorial ceremony for the establishment of the revolutionary government, and discussed preparations for the commemoration of the birth of Shennong, the ancestor of agriculture. Kong Xiangxi

Is Concerned About the Expelled Overseas Chinese in Mexico

And Advocates Serious Negotiations with the Mexican Authorities

Regarding the expulsion of Chinese from Mexico, more than 10,000 overseas Chinese in Mexico are being expelled to China one after another. The Shanghai Golden Globe Overseas Chinese General Association, in order to alleviate the suffering of the afflicted overseas Chinese compatriots, has launched a relief effort to seek temporary solutions, and plans to ask the government to establish overseas Chinese factories to specifically accommodate the unemployed overseas Chinese who have suffered. Yesterday, Peng Canguang, the general manager of the association, visited Kong Xiangxi, the newly appointed president of the Central Bank, who has just returned from overseas and must have a deep understanding of the situation of overseas Chinese. Mr. Kong personally received him and expressed his great sympathy for the distressed overseas Chinese in Mexico. He advocated that the government strictly order Feng Chongzhi, the ambassador to Mexico, to conduct serious negotiations to alleviate the suffering of overseas Chinese. Mr. Kong also promised to do his best to assist in the relief of distressed overseas Chinese.

Sends Hu Zushun to the North to Promote

丨And Contact to Organize Branches丨

The Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association yesterday sent letters to Yu Xiaohou, chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, Han Xiangfang, chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, Mr. Feng Huanzhang of Zhangjiakou, the Tianjin Local Association, the Tianjin Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association, the Tianjin General Chamber of Commerce, the Jinan General Chamber of Commerce, and others, introducing Hu Yuzhai, a standing director of the association, to go to North China to promote the organization of support association branches. Their ultimate intention is to destroy our country and exterminate our nation. At this extraordinary time for our country, we should all rise up together to save ourselves from danger. Our association has been assisting the volunteer army for a year, and the task is arduous. We can only do our best. In the future, the anti-Japanese work will be at the forefront in North China, and the volunteer army in the interior of the eastern provinces still needs practical assistance. Therefore, at the 140th Standing Committee meeting, it was decided to publicly recommend Mr. Hu Zushun to go to North China to promote the organization of volunteer army support branches. We have always admired (your Taiwan seat is a pillar of the country, a pillar in the middle stream), and your association leads the masses and has a far-reaching reputation. You have a sincere enthusiasm for resisting Japan and saving the country. Therefore, we have prepared this letter to inform you. We hope you will investigate and assist, and we implore you to strongly support Mr. Hu's work so that it can proceed smoothly. We are deeply grateful."

Liang Shiyi Was Buried Yesterday

And Returned to Guangdong for Burial

The death of former Prime Minister Liang Shiyi in Shanghai has been reported in previous newspapers. The funeral was held yesterday and the body was returned to Guangdong. At 2:30 pm, the funeral procession departed from his residence on Maqi Road. The Municipal Council sent horse patrols and a motorcade, and the Public Security Bureau sent a police brigade and secret agents to provide protection. All the ceremonial guards followed family instructions and were not ostentatious. The hearse was rented from the Chinese Funeral Parlor. The guests who came to see him off included people from the industrial and commercial sectors such as Zhu Qiqian, the transportation sector such as Ye Gongchuo, the academic sector such as Zheng Hongnian, the banking sector such as Feng Gengguang and Hu Mengjia, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, fellow Guangdong villagers, and friends and former subordinates from Chinese and foreign circles, totaling about 500 people. They all traveled by car, so traffic on the roads was intermittently interrupted. Liang's hearse arrived at the Gonghexiang Wharf, where a public memorial service was held. After the ceremony, the coffin was loaded onto a Jardine Matheson Company ship and sailed directly to Guangzhou, where it was transferred to his hometown in Sanshui for burial. His family accompanied the coffin. Foreigners and film companies took photos of the hearse as it passed, which was extremely honorable.

First Special District

Municipal Federation Schedules Inspection of Enemy Goods

Investigation to Begin on the 15th of This Month

Rules of Service for Investigators Agreed Upon

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens Federation held its fifth Standing Committee meeting at 3:00 pm yesterday. Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, Chen Binghui, Cao Zhigong, and Chen Jiufeng, Wang Chongtang, Liu Zhongying, and Zhu Zhichun of the National Products Movement Committee, totaling more than ten people, attended. Zhang Yichen chaired the meeting and Zheng Dongshan took the minutes. After the usual formalities, the chairman reported on the resolutions of the previous meeting and the progress made. Then, the discussion of various proposals began, and the rules of investigation for enemy goods were approved. The details are as follows:

Resolutions

(1) The proposal to review and approve the rules of service for investigators was read by the chairman and passed item by item. (2) The proposal to establish a secret reporting box (resolved) will be set up in this association. (3) The proposal for the steps to be taken for the investigation (resolved) will first start with the committee members of each district branch. (4) The proposal to convene an investigation committee to discuss the investigation methods (resolved) will be held on the 8th of this month. (5) The proposal for the date of the start of the investigation (resolved) will be set on the 15th of this month. (6) The proposal on how to deal with a certain dyeing company that produces disguised domestic goods based on a secret report (resolved) was referred to Zhang Yichen, Chen Jiufeng, Cao Zhigong, Zhu Zhichun, and Fang Peicheng to conduct a preliminary investigation.

Rules of Investigation

Rules of Service for Investigators: (Article 1) Investigators of the National Products Movement Committee must abide by the provisions of these rules. (Article 2) Investigators must strictly follow the instructions of the Standing Committee members of this association and the supervision of the Investigation Committee. (Article 3) When on duty, investigators must go through the swearing-in procedures. The swearing-in ceremony will be supervised by personnel sent by the First Special District Citizens Federation. (Article 4) If investigators believe that it is necessary to investigate any manufacturers, they must first report to this committee for approval by the Standing Committee before starting the investigation. No direct investigation is allowed to avoid disputes. (Article 5) When investigators visit manufacturers, they must first present the notification issued by this association to show their seriousness. (Article 6) Investigators must strictly keep confidential all matters of this association. (Article 7) After completing the investigation, investigators must prepare an investigation report to facilitate assessment and handling. (Article 8) Investigators are only responsible for the investigation. They may not dispose of goods themselves, except when the Standing Committee has set up a method to be executed. (Article 9) Investigators who violate the discipline of this association will be severely punished. Those who are loyal to their duties and have excellent performance will be rewarded. (Article 10) These rules will be implemented after being resolved by this meeting.

Methods of Adjusting Regeneration 3

— Zheng Zhongtao

For a radio receiver with fewer than three vacuum tubes, adding a regeneration coil can significantly increase reception efficiency. Now, let's discuss how to adjust regeneration. There are four methods for adjusting regeneration:

1. Adjustable Regeneration Coil Method

2. Adjustable Capacitor Method

3. Resistance Adjustment

4. Filament Adjustment

Let me describe them in order.

Adjustable Regeneration Coil Method: This method employs an adjustable regeneration coil to regulate regeneration by varying the distance or orientation between the regeneration coil and the secondary coil, thereby controlling the magnitude of inductive force. Commonly sold drum-type three-circuit coils and spider-web coil frames fall into this category. With a drum-type coil, when the regeneration coil and secondary coil are parallel, induction is at its maximum, resulting in the strongest regeneration. When they are at right angles, induction is minimal, and regeneration is weakest. (If the situation is reversed, it's due to the regeneration coil being connected backward and should be reconnected.) As for the spider-web type, the magnitude of regeneration is determined by the distance between the coils. See circuit diagram Figure 1.

Adjustable Capacitor Method: The previous adjustment method is not very convenient. If the regeneration coil and secondary coil positions are fixed, an adjustable capacitor is added, with a capacitance of 0.00035 or 0.0005 microfarads (μF). (The value should be determined by the number of turns in the coil; more turns require a smaller capacitance, and fewer turns require a larger capacitance.) The wiring method involves connecting one end of the regeneration coil to the earphone post and also to the fixed plate of the capacitor; the adjustable plate of the capacitor is connected to the negative terminal of the B battery and grounded. Figures 2 and 3 illustrate the circuit diagrams. The difference in the lower diagram is the addition of a high-frequency choke at the earphone connection to reduce noise.

Resistance Adjustment Method: The magnitude of regeneration is directly proportional to the plate current. Therefore, adding a 500,000-ohm adjustable resistor between the earphone and the positive terminal of the B battery can be used to adjust regeneration. Resistance and voltage are inversely proportional, and voltage and current are directly proportional. Thus, we can adjust the plate voltage by varying the resistance, and then adjust regeneration through the relationship between plate voltage and plate current. See circuit diagram Figure 4. In the diagram, the 1-microfarad fixed capacitor is used to prevent noise caused by unstable contact between the adjustable handle and the resistor part of the adjustable resistor.

Filament Adjustment Method: This method is based on the same principle as the previous method, but it uses the brightness of the filament to control the current strength, thereby adjusting regeneration. The filament rheostat used for regeneration adjustment should have a higher resistance than the usual type; it's best to use a carbon type, referred to in English as a CARBON PIT RHEOSTATE. See Figure 5.

Based on the author's experience, the second and third methods mentioned above are easier to adjust and most efficient. There are other methods, but they are omitted here for brevity.

Power Transformer Manufacturing Method (Continued) 4

— Xin

The ratio of the output power to the input power at the primary input is called efficiency, often expressed as a percentage, as follows:

The efficiency of each transformer in the table is determined by actual experiments and is very practical.

Find a transformer with a 50-watt input in the table and multiply by the efficiency of that transformer, then the output number should be:

50 × 0.75 = 37.5 watts

If the output of the transformer in the example is 34 watts, which is less than the above number, it is safer to use a 50-watt transformer.

The primary input is 50 watts, connected to a 200-volt power line, so the current passing through the coil can be known, and the wire number can be determined. The formula for calculating the current is as follows:

The wire number to be used can be found in the second table. The primary uses 24 gauge wire (B. S.)

Secondary (1) uses 14 gauge wire (two strands in parallel)

(2) 15 or 14 gauge wire

(3) 34 gauge wire

Second table

The number of turns of the transformer can be obtained by multiplying the number of turns per volt by the number of volts.

Primary turns: 4.8 × 220 = 1056 turns (same as in the table)

Secondary turns (1): 4.8 × 2.5 = 12 turns

(2) 4.8 × 5 = 24 turns

(3) 4.8 × 600 = 2880 turns (draw out a tap in 1440 turns, i.e., the center line)

It is best to use silicon steel sheets shaped like the Chinese character "山" (mountain) for the iron core, but this kind of sheet is very expensive. The iron skin of gasoline cans can also be used, cut into the shape of "山" to replace it. The size of the iron core of the example transformer is shown in Figure 2. The iron cores of other transformers can be imitated accordingly.

After the iron core is cut, apply a thin layer of varnish or enamel on it to avoid eddy current loss. Then make a frame with thick paper as shown in the third figure. After it is made, you can wind the wire. First wind the secondary coil, then wind the high-voltage secondary coil, and wind the low-voltage secondary coil on the outermost layer. The wire must be wound very neatly, with wax paper separating each layer, especially several layers between the primary and secondary to prevent leakage. It is advisable to use enameled wire, because it can withstand higher voltage and takes up less space. After the wire is completely wound, immerse it completely in candle oil and fry it to prevent moisture. Then insert the iron cores opposite each other to form a perfect transformer! (The End)

Small Experiences

Lightweight and Convenient Shielding Cover 5

— Li Yuanqing

The metal shielding covers commonly used in radios are generally made of aluminum, which is difficult to make by yourself. If you accumulate many discarded cigarette tin foils and paste them in the middle of two layers of drawing paper (as shown in the figure), it is a very good shielding cover.

Don't Wear Gold Rings, Wear Copper Rings. Li Yuanqing

Bend the copper sheet as shown in the figure on the left, and file a thin slot in the middle. When winding the coil, putting it on your thumb can get a lot of convenience and satisfactory results. Zero News

Three Hundred People Compete for a Bowl of Rice 6

— Qi

A private radio station in Paris posted an advertisement for one reporter, and three hundred people applied, including five women, one architect, and many lawyers and writers. The initial test eliminated two hundred and seventy people, and the retest reduced the remainder to twelve people. Finally, a special selection committee selected six people to try broadcasting, and the audience voted to determine the final candidate. Alas, it is also difficult to seek a career! ()

Radios All Over the World 7

— Songfu

Recently, Mr. BOULGET, an investigator of the British Broadcasting Wireless Radio Company, made a very precise survey of all radios in the world today. Statistics show that there are about 31 million radios in the world. The distribution is as follows:

Europe has a total of 15,292,000 sets. The United Kingdom has 3,941,200 sets; Germany has 3,564,800 sets; France has 2,345,790 sets; Soviet Russia has 1,964,200 sets; and other countries have about 3,476,010 sets.

The Americas have a total of 13,353,280 sets. The United States has 11,567,800 sets; Canada has 382,680 sets; Mexico has 150,000 sets; Argentina has 450,000 sets; Brazil has 200,000 sets; and South America has 602,880 sets.

Asia has a total of 1,050,000 sets. (Of which Japan accounts for 859,520 sets; China is unknown) Australia has a total of 354,684 sets. Africa has 49,928 sets. The Union of South Africa accounts for 30,000 sets; Algeria has 15,400 sets; and others have 4,528 sets.

The United States Will Establish a Third Broadcasting Network 8

— Qi

According to a Reuter's dispatch, there are currently two major broadcasting companies in the United States, one is the National Broadcasting Company founded in 1926, and the other is the Columbia Broadcasting Company founded in 1927. In the near future, a third major broadcasting company may be established. The originator is Mr. Edwin, a comedian who is well-known in the American broadcasting industry. The required funds will be borne by local wealthy gentlemen. Several major companies have expressed their willingness to cooperate with the company as a means of broadcasting advertisements. When this new organization is established in the future, its broadcasting network will spread throughout the country, forming a tripartite with the two existing broadcasting networks, and competition will be inevitable.

A Method to Avoid Interference: Shielding the Lead-In Wire 10

— VT

The structure of the antenna has a significant relationship to eliminating radio station interference and various disturbances during radio reception. This is an undeniable fact. Interference can be roughly divided into three types: one is atmospheric interference, which people cannot avoid; the second is interference generated by the operation of electrical machinery; and the third is mutual interference of radio waves emitted by most radio stations. We can remedy and avoid this through the special structure of the antenna.

The remedy is to use a short vertical antenna, only ten feet long, installed at the highest point of the roof. The lead-in wire used is a shielded lead-in wire (SCREENED LEAD IN WIRE), which is to shield the lead-in wire and ground it). At the same time, special attention must be paid to the internal wiring of the radio, and the grounding must be particularly perfect. The radio itself must also be shielded. If necessary, a filter can also be used.

That the antenna is as short as ten feet is not a problem, since modern radio construction is becoming more and more perfect. However, in order to increase reception performance, the capacitance of the antenna should not be too small. The method of increasing its capacitance has always been to increase the number of antenna roots, but increasing the number of antenna roots will still increase interference. Therefore, we should use a spiral antenna to increase the length. In this way, the capacitance can be increased, and the interference from radio stations can be avoided as much as possible.

A. Antenna, B. Shielded lead-in wire solder joint C. Shielded lead-in wire

D. Grounding

A well-known repair company at sea had repaired it, and said that according to the circuit diagram of the machine body, there were no flaws to be found. It is no coincidence that Yada Company's radio receiver repair department can stand out from the crowd in the radio receiver repair industry in Shanghai.

Spring and Autumn

Doubts About Anti-British Slogans in Tokyo 11

— Zhanlu

The anti-British fervor in Tokyo is hotter than the "so hot that the dwarves jump" sung in the vegetarian meal variety shows! Just look at the black, white, and red characters printed on the anti-British slogans pasted on wooden boards, bamboo fences, and telephone poles throughout the city. A kind of stomping and resentment almost made them stomp their wooden clogs into pieces! Especially the slogans "Britain disregards Anglo-Japanese friendship and repays kindness with hatred." and "Gather the 400 million Chinese and 300 million Indians to drive out British forces to the west of the Suez Canal." The former is like a young woman resenting her lover, and the latter is like a shrew scolding in the street; but, I wonder if the British got this news, were they frightened or just laughed it off?

Laugh or jump? Let's not worry about that for now; but, looking at these two slogans with a calm eye, I can't help but have the following two doubts:

Do your citizens also know about friendship? Do they also know the boundaries of resentment and virtue? Let me ask, does the relationship between China and your country not qualify for the word "friend"? Your culture is completely derived from China. Spiritually and materially, you have received a lot of help from China. Does your country, when drinking water, think of its source, and has it forgotten China's great virtue? The Zhu Ming Dynasty, your country repeatedly harassed our maritime borders, not to mention that. In recent decades, we have not invaded your country, but your country has repeatedly launched military campaigns, ceded Ryukyu, destroyed Goryeo, demanded Taiwan, and swallowed Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol. Is this not repaying kindness with hatred?

Your country wants to drive the British to the west of the Suez Canal, I'm afraid that "drinking up the entire West River in one gulp" is not going to happen. Even if this happened, our 400 million people who have been ravaged by your country would actually be on the list of participants, which is a bit flattering. Since you are cooperating with the Chinese, why are you destroying the Chinese? If it is said that we are both in Asia and of the same yellow race, there is a possibility of cooperation; why, since the September 18th Incident, have we only seen your countrymen secretly flirting with the Europeans, and only wantonly used the most vicious artillery and aircraft to wreak havoc on the Chinese of the same continent and race? Posting slogans is your country's freedom; but, it is not too funny to write the 400 million Chinese on it as well?

The End of the Road 12

— Zui Chisheng

When a person reaches the point of "plans exhausted, assistance cut off, and nothing can be done," it is called "the end of the road." Therefore, "the end of the road" is the last stop of a person's life and career. From the literal meaning, it naturally contains full of sorrow and desolation.

The end of the road for a businessman is bankruptcy. The end of the road for the poor and those who are brokenhearted is suicide. The end of the road for criminals is imprisonment! Execution. The end of the road for the defeated is surrender; submission.

Only the end of the road for the rich and the military is unusual. Their end of the road is "going abroad." Once they are dismissed from their posts and out of office, forced by the environment, they walk to a foreign country. Whether it is for investigation or for recuperation, they always spend their years leisurely, and can somewhat absorb some fresh air from Europe. When they are happy and come back, the capital is originally Mack Mack, and they are still no less than a "rich man." Or they can still be called "an old man." Alas! The end of the road for the rich and the military is exactly the "end of the road" that ordinary people dream of and admire so much.

Ticks On the Market 13

— A Jie

"Really annoying, Aunt Wang from next door is coming again! Eating a little doesn't matter, but once she starts talking, it's a headache to listen to!" This is what my grandmother often said at lunch and snack time. It turns out that Aunt Wang, my neighbor, is the reincarnation of Grandma Liu in the Dream of the Red Chamber. She has a mouth that can talk. Another characteristic is that when she sees smoke coming out of someone's chimney, or hears the sound of cooking in a pot, she will definitely come to my house. Of course, when she sees our elderly grandmother, she wants to start talking, talking about the east and the west, and not stopping. We have already brought up lunch or snacks at this time, of course, we can't let Aunt Wang sit alone in the corner. She is also not to be outdone, sits down with a thump, and eats a full stomach. While gobbling down food, she talked about the Classics of Mountains and Seas. First, she chanted "Amitabha," and then smeared her mouth and said, "The mother of the eldest, was caught in adultery last night: the daughter-in-law of the second eldest, stole a man and ran away." Piece by piece, she reported the scandals in society to my grandmother, like an outside reporter in a newspaper. After eating, Aunt Wang wiped her mouth, and the conversation stopped from then on. She will have to wait until tomorrow or the day after tomorrow, when the smoke comes out of our chimney and the sound of pots and pans sounds again, and she will come to our humble house again and start her mouth work.

These days, ticks are on the market, so I am reminded of Aunt Wang when I was a child. It's really strange, we spent half a day in the corner of the bed and on the top of the tent doing the work of suppressing bandits, hoping to wipe them all out, eliminate the red bandits, and live a peaceful life in peace and stability, and be peaceful people. How could we know that they appear and disappear unpredictably, decentralize and integrate, and it is really not easy to pacify them! Because we cannot sleep well at night, we cannot do things during the day; therefore, "resisting foreign aggression" must first "pacify the interior," which is a military strategy that is justified. For example, in a few days, poisonous mosquitoes will suck our blood. As long as we keep the tent tightly closed and have this Great Wall-like national defense, we will not be invaded by poisonous mosquitoes and can rest easy. Only the ticks in the cracks of the bed are the most difficult internal troubles to solve! Therefore, "resisting foreign aggression" must first "pacify the interior," and the work of catching ticks is more important than the work of exterminating poisonous mosquitoes; therefore, I put aside poisonous mosquitoes and only talk about ticks.

It is said that ticks have very sensitive hearing and sense of smell. We cannot hear the sound of our own blood flowing in our bodies, but in the ears of ticks, it is like the tide of the Yangtze River surging and surging. We don't smell our own armpit odor, bad breath, bullhead odor, etc., and we are proud that our whole body is fragrant and fragrant, and our breath is like orchid: but when it blows into the nose of a tick, it naturally understands, and of course it will cling to the smelly like ants on rotten meat. Ticks have this ability, just like fleas. To compare the jumping ability of fleas to humans, isn't it able to jump over the roof of Sassoon? These are all unique gifts given to insects by nature, there is no need to envy and admire them. Only our good neighbor Aunt Wang is like this!

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 14

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Six: Coldly Observe the Sweet and Bitter Love Scene, Assess Both Sides; Secret Agreement for Three Years on the Rugged Worldly Road

Guan Yaowu jumped up and said: Don't make trouble, don't make trouble, isn't this buying it for you? It's really killing me, seeing one load and buying one load. As he spoke, he turned his head casually and smiled: Your two uncles are here, hurry up and wish them a happy New Year. The child in his arms heard this, put his two little palms together, bowed, and made a New Year's greeting in his father's arms. The two older ones only hid behind their father. Zhao Ziqiang touched the child's head, said a few words with a smile, took out some money, bought two sugar figurines for each of the children, and then went into the house. Yin Deren smiled and said: Our Big Brother Guan is so busy in the camp, and when he comes home, he is incredibly busy. Guan Yaowu sighed and said: There's no way! Your sister-in-law is alone, except for my eldest son, she has to take care of these three children, and also do the laundry and cooking, which is really enough for her. When I come back, I feel a little bad. I always have to help her a little. As he spoke, he led the two of them into the house. They lived in the three northern houses in the middle. In the middle room, there was also a table for offering sacrifices to the gods, and the ground was covered with sesame stalks for stepping on the year. However, there were also children's toys, small gongs, small drums, small knives and spears, as well as pieces of wet poop that had fallen and not been picked up. The adults used a basin of leftover filling, and a white coal stove. On the tea table were hard seeds wrapped in miscellaneous things, and on the chairs were ivory dominoes, sesame candy, and a foreign iron kettle. Guan Yaowu stood in the middle of the room and shouted: Come on! Look, what a mess this room is in. Where is our eldest son? Let him come and sweep the floor. Someone in the room replied: It's not after the third day of the new year yet, how can you sweep the floor? Guan Yaowu said: There are so many children in our family, it's always enough to make a mess. The sesame stalks that have fallen on the ground are simply... Before he could finish speaking, the voice in the room was twice as loud and said: What do you know? It's because there are children in the family that we bought sesame stalks to step on the year. Is it for you, a person as big as you, to use? Zhao Ziqiang had just entered the door and caused a quarrel in someone else's family, which was a bit embarrassing, so he interrupted and said: Sister-in-law, please come out, we're here to wish you a happy New Year. The person inside the room was Guan Yaowu's wife, Yuan Shi. (61)

Shanghai Night Talk 15

— Zhang Ruochun

Crystal Palace

Every day at dusk, I hang my cane and stroll along the sidewalk on Avenue Joffre, accustomed to the decorations of the shops on both sides. One evening, near Rue Cardinal Mercier, I unexpectedly discovered a novel window. Inside the tall, transparent glass window were displayed many shell-shaped soda bottles, alternating in red and white. The nickel-plated caps and accessories on the bottles reflected dazzling electric light, capturing the attention of passersby.

A right-angled white-lacquered counter was filled with glass bottles of all sizes. Through the gaps between the glittering containers holding mineral water, the beautiful figure of a young woman in white emerged. Everything was white-lacquered, silver, and glass, completely evoking the atmosphere of an open-air ice-drinking place by the summer seaside.

I and a friend who had just returned from Vienna, along with another friend wearing a new silver-gray flannel suit, chose seats near the road and sat down in the white-lacquered rattan chairs with streamlined designs. We looked around in amazement, realizing that there was neither coffee nor beer here. The sign told us that this was a place exclusively selling "Shada Mineral Water," so we ordered three glasses of mineral water from the unique waitress.

The blonde, blue-eyed waitress served three glasses of fruit-flavored mineral water of different colors. The one as red as a woman's cherry lips was plum juice; the orange-yellow one like kumquat was lemon. I chose a glass of soapy liquid, distinguishing the exquisite taste of chocolate on the tip of my tongue.

Whether it was psychological or scientific, we found that the taste of the mineral water was indeed somewhat different from ordinary soda water or filtered water. The texture of the mineral water seemed thick and cold. I had drunk Huiquan spring water from Wuxi and tasted spring tea from Hupao Temple in Hangzhou. Huiquan spring water and spring tea are brewed with spring water, so they felt clear, fragrant, and slightly bitter. This mineral water was mixed with fruit juice, so it only felt sweet and cool to the heart.

Above our heads were four stage-like electric lights, emitting strong white light. We were like film actors performing under crystal lights, gazing at the pedestrians on the street through the glass window, seeing only vague, dreamlike shadows. We quietly smoked cigarettes, surrounded by bright, shimmering glass windows and mirrors, as if we were in a crystal palace from a fairy tale or a beautiful legend.

The cigarette gradually burned down, and the mineral water in the glasses slowly receded like the tide. Our conversation began.

A: "Mr. So-and-so's elegant hobby is truly admirable. He recently published correspondence with a female student who calls herself Little Devil. Have you seen it?"

B: "No, it's just a nauseating attempt at humor. There's nothing to see."

C: "Those aren't ordinary love letters. That female student is the woman who bore Mr. So-and-so's child. You must see it."

B: "At most, it's just something to amuse the poor."

A: "Don't underestimate him. Mr. So-and-so has his own extraordinary greatness. His greatness is that he feels he is a good person when hated by the people he hates."

C: "In my opinion, Mr. So-and-so's only merit is that he always sees everything Chinese, every word and deed, in the worst possible light. What the Chinese say is good, he always thinks is bad. What the Chinese hate, he insists is good."

A: "This isn't his insensitivity. His liking to think in the worst way proves that he loves the Chinese. It's like, the more he loves, the more he hates."

B: "When Mr. So-and-so speaks, people find it laughable, but he himself doesn't laugh. Why is that?"

C: "Because the Chinese are laughable."

A: "When Bernard Shaw came to Shanghai, Shaw smiled. Didn't Mr. So-and-so also smile along? If you don't believe me, there are photos to prove it."

B: "If Mr. So-and-so truly liked Shaw for the reason of 'the more he loves, the more he hates,' he should have slapped Shaw in the face."

An hour passed in this way.

Continued Records of the Silkworm Season in Su and Zhejiang

Wujin

Wujin in Jiangsu Province is also the most prosperous area for silkworm rearing. There are more than 200 cocoon shops in the whole county. The cocoon production in each session is no less than that of Wuxi. In recent years, due to the damage caused by the weather, the silkworm affairs have repeatedly failed. This year, the price of rice is also cheap, and the spring season is winter, and the small harvest is disappointing. The rural economy is bankrupt, and there is no capital to purchase seeds. In addition, the late spring cold rain lasts for more than ten days, and the germination of mulberry plants is relatively late, so the spring silkworms in the four villages are unusually silent. Fortunately, the weather turned clear later, and the farmers who planted mulberry trees borrowed money and capital to purchase seeds and hatch them. The amount of feeding is smooth in the areas of Henglin Qishuyan in the east, and there are many who feed foreign species. There are interplanted earth species in the west villages. The temperature is suitable, and the ants are collected quite neatly. The early gangs in the west villages have been opening leaves for many days, and the late gangs in the east villages are still trying leaves,

Haining

The native species of early gangs in Haining, Zhejiang Province, have been discarded in 78/10 this year due to economic and weather reasons. Afterwards, the weather turned better, and the farmers borrowed silkworm capital to increase the purchase of improved species and engaged in hatching and collecting ants. After that, the climate was suitable, and the silkworm ants developed smoothly. The early gangs of improved species silkworms have been in good condition and have been leaf-eating for three sleeps, and the late gangs will also start sleeping. The temperature has been lower in the past two days, and there has been cloudy rain, but with the assistance of instructors, the silkworm households have been able to adjust the care. According to reports, some people in Jinshidun and other places are late to wake up from sleep. Although the tea merchants have been insisting, they have been weak, so they are all holding a wait-and-see attitude. Therefore, the new teas from Wenzhou, Sui'an, and local villages have been listed one after another, and the new disks have not been opened. Hope and Luck 16

— Xia Ying

In these times when economic panic is rampant throughout the world, even reducing one bowl of rice per meal, a necessity of life, is a good thing. As for luxury goods that do not fill the stomach, it is natural to economize on them, or to use those of poorer quality and lower price.

However, those commodities that used to sell well and were relatively expensive, aren't they "piled up like mountains" and rotting in warehouses because everyone is economizing? Selling at a loss regardless of the cost is not a game. After deep thought and deliberation, the capitalists say a beautiful thing: It's not difficult for us to shut down the factories and auction off the inventory, but the unemployment of the workers is a major social problem!

Therefore, they are taking advantage of the crowd's gambling mentality in a declining society, coming up with all sorts of "prize coupons" and "cash rewards."

Thus, even students and young ladies who used to smoke cigarettes are buying two packs of domestically produced White Gold Dragon cigarettes to participate in the poetry riddle contest, hoping to win the first prize, "500 yuan in cash."

Workers who have never used any kind of perfumed soap to wash their faces are also saving their meal money to buy a few bars of Palm Soap, cutting out the fragments of airplanes, towers, butterflies, roosters, rabbits, etc. from the newspaper and gluing them onto a white sheet of paper, hoping to win a radio. Or, instead of participating in a free three-day tour of Putuo and Suzhou, they can redeem it for dozens of yuan in cash.

It is said that the government-issued aviation lottery tickets have already gone on sale. Several people must pool their money to buy a ticket and dream a golden dream. If they have the money, shouldn't Italy, Switzerland, and France be open for everyone to travel, not just the "big shots"? Everyone should lie on their backs, face up, on their beds and hope!

Hope and luck are our Chinese spiritual civilization. Hoping that the Japanese soldiers will automatically withdraw from the Great Wall, withdraw from Rehe and the three northeastern provinces. Heaven has eyes and should sink the three islands of Japan! Japan is originally an island nation prone to earthquakes!

Feinting East and Attacking West 17

— Xu

In Chinese strategic terms, in contrast to "pacifying the interior and resisting foreign aggression," there is also a tactic called "feinting east and attacking west." The Japanese imperialist army's invasion is clearly in the Northeast, but the direction of the Chinese army is deliberately not towards that area. What is particularly unpredictable and baffling is the defense plan in the southwest. If the attack comes from the Northeast, I think no matter how large the cannons are, one shot now, one shot now, they still can't hit the southwest, but defensive fortifications are already being built on the southwestern border.

This kind of Chinese strategy of "feinting east and attacking west" is not only useful in actual combat, but also in general declarations. Please see the "Letter to Workers from the Municipal General Labor Union" on May 1st, which first says to unite and unite to overthrow the aggression of international capitalism and resist the unreasonable oppression of domestic capitalists; then it says that China's production is backward and that we must endure hardship and work hard to reduce production costs; finally, it particularly emphasizes sharing the difficulties and striving for sincere cooperation between labor and capital (see the Shanghai News section of the May 1st Shen Bao).

Foreigners also use this tactic in political warfare, commercial warfare, or other battlefields, but they use it more skillfully than the Chinese, making it difficult to see the underlying reasons at a glance. For example, Japan clearly has ambitions to annex Chahar and Suiyuan, and occupy Beiping and Tianjin, and is actively plotting in secret, but Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi's words to reporters say that the attitude Japan is currently taking is one of quiet observation, generally meaning that Japan is neither fighting nor negotiating with China. Austria's repair of tens of thousands of guns for Italy seems to be just a commercial transaction on the surface, but in reality, it has long been seen through by Britain and France, who have lodged a protest, saying that in order to maintain peace in Europe and implement disarmament among nations, they have to take this tough stance.

The strategy of "feinting east and attacking west" is used both in China and abroad, but it seems that the Chinese only use it internally, while foreigners use it exclusively externally, with only this one difference.

Random Notes on Moving (Continued) 18

— Yu Dafu

As I wandered and thought on the street, my footsteps unconsciously reversed, and after a few turns, I actually moved my own body to a road near the university. Looking ahead, there was another pile of earthen hills. Below the hills were flat dirt roads and shallow ponds. I had come to this area when I was a child. More than twenty years ago, I had a relative who had served as an officer in Baoguo Temple, and I had an older brother who had been a student in the Army Elementary School. Since I had already returned to the vicinity of my residence, I might as well climb up the hill and take a look. After not sleeping all night, my mind was still a bit muddled, and ascending to a height to look around might not be a bad way to clear my head.

The weather was also gradually clearing up, and in the southeastern half, a few patches of blue sky and a trace of sunlight had actually appeared. Although the earthen hills were not high, the view was not bad. The mountains on the lake surrounded the northwest area, and further north was empty space, and even further north were the hair-like green mountains in Huzhou. Far to the east, the visible peaks were Lianping Mountain, Gaoting Mountain, Huanghe Mountain, and the like. A little more to the northeast, it was probably the shadow of Chao Mountain in Tangqi. Although it didn't seem far away, it would probably take half a day to walk there. After looking around on the earthen hills, from far to near, I finally understood the geography of this area by calculating with a mass observation method. It turned out that my new residence was to the north of the Ordnance Bureau, and the earthen hills on three sides were remotely connected to the city walls, surrounding the Ordnance Bureau. No wonder I heard a burst of bugle calls at dawn today, and no wonder I saw a guard soldier standing upright with a gun when I walked out of the new residence.

"Very good! Very good!..." I thought in my heart, "With books in front and an armory in the back, the way of the civilian and the military is complete here!" Although I was amusing myself in this way in my heart, a feeling of decline, a sorrow of not being able to gain a foothold in the metropolis again, gradually permeated my whole body. (The End)

May 19

— Zhou Muzhai

May has arrived, and the time has come for Japan and China to settle accounts.

In the lunar calendar, this month is said to be a poisonous month, and the fifth day of the month is the most poisonous day of the poisonous month, designated as the Dragon Boat Festival, with paper charms, mugwort swords, Zhong Kui images hanging, and realgar wine drunk, all said to be used to ward off evil and eliminate disasters.

In the current calendar, there are "May 3rd," "May 4th," "May 5th" (note), "May 7th," "May 9th," "May 30th," and other memorial days that are fragments of memorial days, pieced together into a confused account of May. On each memorial day, memorial meetings are held as usual, with Sun Yat-sen's portrait hung, slogans posted, and calls shouted, and sometimes a day off is also taken. The creditors of these many memorial days are all, or partially, related to Japan, and the routine work of each memorial day is probably to overthrow "Eastern devils" or "dwarf devils."

Using old Chinese sayings to express the difference between the two: the object of the Dragon Boat Festival can be said to be "natural disasters," and the purpose can be said to be "protecting the home"; the object of various memorial days is "man-made disasters," and the purpose is "saving the nation."

"Natural disasters" are long-term, and "long-term resistance" requires sustained strength, so first of all, we must "prepare for resistance"丨丨no, "preparing for resistance" is "long-term resistance," stimulating and storing strength. In this way, the poisonous month becomes a festive season. The stimulating realgar wine and the condensing glutinous rice dumplings have different functions here, but they complement each other. Although they don't know "protecting the home without forgetting entertainment," they can also say things like "harmony brings auspiciousness." From this point of view, long-term resistance is not an invention of modern people, but a traditional Chinese art.

Ancient substance, modern style, modern people should of course be more skillful. Taking a holiday on memorial days can be said to be "studying without forgetting saving the nation." This is the first movement. The original meaning of memorial days is to inject new life into dead bones, but now they want to get some stimulation from dead bones. Saving the nation must first save oneself, saving oneself must first save the heart, so we wander and roam, "entertaining to save the nation." This is the second movement. Excessive stimulation leads to麻醉. The initial appearance of stimulation is tension, is urging, although tension is momentary, the one being urged has had enough: things have roots and branches, returning to the true and the simple, naturally must be restored: "saving the nation without forgetting reading." This is the third movement. Excessive tension results in "calm."

The lunar May is nominally abolished; what about the confused account of the current May?

(Note) Refers to the Shanghai Truce Agreement of 1932.

Little Lotus 20

— Wang Wanrong

Although the peach blossoms have fallen, fortunately the bauhinia flowers are in full bloom, and soon the fragrant lilacs will replace the showy bauhinia. Walking out of the northern city, the road is crowded with men and women enjoying the spring. The waterfall of Peach Blossom Stream rushes forward incessantly, and several children in red clothes are laughing at the splashing water. The moving laughter follows the flowing water far away. In the azure sky, white clouds float, and the cuckoo's cry tells us that spring is deep.

Climbing over the large stone engraved with the three red characters "Peach Blossom Stream," and then turning past a very tall chaste chastity arch, a desolate tomb appears in the clusters of pines, cypresses, and chestnut trees. Although today is Qingming Festival, there is no paper ash or fresh flowers to be found in front of the tomb, and even less anyone weeping or sighing there. Only a pair of cuckoos are singing sadly on the branches. The clear sound of the flowing water of Peach Blossom Stream transmits to this quiet realm.

Walking to the front of the tomb, behind the tomb is a stone tablet, the writing on the tablet is already blurred, but after careful identification, one can still see the five characters: "Tomb of Little Lotus." "Little Lotus, who is she?" I wondered. At the same time, the shadow of a sallow little girl flickered before my eyes.

Little Lotus was a child who sold her skills, she followed her parents and companions,摇着boat around various places, and always came to my hometown several times a year. The boat happened to stop at a dock outside the window of the study, and I often heard her companions calling her that, so I knew that "Little Lotus" was her beautiful name.

As long as that dilapidated white wooden boat docked outside the window, I would start to get busy. Not to mention going to school, I even lacked the mood to eat, and all day I would lie on the window throwing some fruit onto their boat, teasing that monkey in the red clothes. As usual, around ten o'clock in the morning, they would have lunch, and after that they would tidy everything up. Little Lotus's father, that middle-aged man, and two young men, carried the boxes and other necessary items, Little Lotus's mother squatted with the monkey in the red clothes, Little Lotus changed into a red jacket and green pants, behind her mother, everyone set off to perform in the open space in front of the Pillow Stone Pavilion teahouse.

Little Lotus's skills were not small, she could stand on the wine bottle that her mother was wobblyly squatting on, she could sing, and she could also do the trick of taking off and putting on clothes on a bamboo pole hanging in mid-air with her pigtails. But that child always had a sallow face, and her body was as tired as a dried chicken. Last year when she came to my hometown she was this sallow and thin, this short, and this year she is still this sallow and thin, this short. It looks like she will always be eleven or twelve years old.

Two years ago, on a New Year's Day, Little Lotus and her parents and companions were brought under my window by that dilapidated white wooden boat again. I lay on the window all day again teasing that monkey in the red clothes. Little Lotus was not only still that sallow and thin, that short, but she was also often seen holding her chest, frowning, and coughing. But she still went ashore to sell her skills every day around ten o'clock in the morning, and returned to the boat around five o'clock in the afternoon.

On this day, at about two o'clock, my brothers and I were playing dice, when suddenly there was a commotion in the quiet pier for a while, and then there was the sound of women crying. I put down the dice, walked into the study, opened the window and looked towards the pier, many onlookers on the pier were discussing. After a while, my younger brother jumped in from outside and said: Little Lotus today stood on the wine bottle that her mother squatted on and sang, but she slipped and fell from a very high place, spat out a few mouthfuls of blood, and died.

In the evening, the sound of nailing coffins and Little Lotus's mother's wailing came from the pier again. The next morning, there was no movement. I pushed open the door and looked out, and the two dilapidated white wooden boats had quietly left the pier at some time.

Year after year, the dilapidated white wooden boat never came again, and the impression of Little Lotus, who was short and thin, holding her chest, frowning, and coughing, disappeared from my mind; who knew that today I would accidentally discover the grave of this pitiful girl on a walk in the spring outing?

Although they are strangers with whom I have no connection, but when I think of that young age, struggling with life, and sleeping in the yellow earth before tasting any sweetness of life, I always have a feeling of "difficult to ask heaven" of melancholy.

I solemnly inserted the bauhinia flowers I picked on the road in front of the tomb: Poor Little Lotus, rest in peace!
