Carrot Top 21

— by JULES RENARD, translated by Lin Qu

Dots and Surfaces

When Lepic was in a good mood, he was very willing to make his children happy himself. When he was walking in the garden, he would tell them stories, sometimes making the eldest son Felix and Carrot Top laugh and roll on the ground. This morning, they were laughing to death again. But the elder sister, Ernestine, ran to tell them that the meal had been served, and they suddenly became quiet. Whenever the family sat together, everyone's faces were always frowning.

Everyone ate quickly and silently as usual, and after a while, everyone except one of the Lepic family had finished eating, at which time the one of the Lepic family said:

"Please give me a little bread to finish spreading my jam!"

Who was she talking to?

Most of the time, the one of the Lepic family always ate alone, so she only talked to the dog. She told it the price of the side dishes, she told it about the difficulty of supporting six people and a dog with a little money at this time.

"No," she said to Pilam, the dog (dog's name), wagging its tail on the grass mat and gurgling affectionately to her, "you really don't know the suffering I endure to support this family. You also think, like those men, that a cook can buy anything with a little money. Of course, you don't care at all if butter goes up in price or eggs are terribly expensive."

However, this time, the one of the Lepic family's attitude was unusual. She addressed her remark directly to Lepic as an exception. This time she was asking him, and indeed asking him, for a little bread to finish spreading her jam. There was no room for doubt about this. First, because she was looking at Lepic when she spoke. Secondly, because the bread was placed in front of Lepic. Lepic was startled at first, he hesitated for a moment, then, with his fingertips, he picked up a little bread from his dirty, eaten dish and threw it to the one of the Lepic family with a very serious and very gloomy face. threw it to the one of the Lepic family.

Was this a comedy, or a tragedy? Who knew?

The elder sister Ernestine felt her mother was humiliated, and felt a vague fear in her heart.

"Dad is very happy to joke around today," the eldest son Felix thought to himself, riding on the back of his chair as if no one was there.

As for Carrot Top, his mouth was full of grease, he kept his mouth tightly closed, his ears were filled with sounds, and his cheeks were swollen with fried sweet potatoes. He was holding back; but if the one of the Lepic family didn't leave the table immediately, he would explode. Because people were treating her like something cheap in front of her son and daughter!

(Correction) In yesterday's Carrot Top, the 36th line "First, I thought I was forbidding him to drink..." was a misprint of "He first thought I was forbidding him to drink...", hereby corrected.

Talk

Explanation of "Side Income" 22

— Xiao Zhi

Living in a realistic society, "side income" has indeed become the lifeline of most people. Yesterday I ran into an old classmate and talked about the problem of life. He told me that he worked in a certain company, with a salary of only twenty dollars a month, but he had the burden of a large family of eight, including servants, and he was able to live a very wealthy and comfortable life. I asked him how he coped, and he said: It all depends on "side income".

The so-called "side income" is the unexpected benefit outside of one's duty. In other words: it is a fluke, a harvest that should not be there and relies on fate: it is a cheap thing with only rights and absolutely no responsibilities. For example: my old classmate, he only gets a salary of twenty dollars a month, so he should only do things within the scope of twenty dollars, and he is not responsible for things outside of twenty dollars. Although his wealthy and comfortable life is ultimately a benefit of the company, because it is "side income," he does not have the obligation to fully bear responsibility. Another example: a corrupt official who desperately scrapes fat from the heads of the people, and he can certainly not have any political achievements. This is because what he scraped is not his due salary, but indeed "side income."

Now let's give a few practical examples to clarify what is called "side income."

On the evening of Shenyang's fall, several thousand "gold bars" from our young Marshal Zhang's family were confiscated by the Japanese. But later, it was said that as soon as Jinzhou was given away, the "gold bars" were returned to their original owner. The young marshal gave away a piece of Jinzhou and regained his "gold bars." This lost and regained "gold bars" is called "side income"; (2) Our young marshal (sorry, I still have to borrow our young marshal here), he lost the Northeast, thus losing his deputy commander-in-chief, pacification director, and acting deputy commissioner, etc. These kinds of official positions, which is certainly a very sad thing. But the young marshal was able to take this opportunity to run to Europe to play foreign golf, inject foreign morphine, hug foreign dancers, ... and bring some priceless antique national treasures with him when he left, auctioning off a naval hospital, of course, these are not insignificant supplements for our young marshal, and these are exactly the "side income" of the young marshal losing his official position; (3) General Tang escaped from Chengde, and many people advocated dragging him out to kill him, but he was finally very fortunate not to die, and now he is also serving as the commander and a certain county magistrate. This "happiness" is of course General Tang's "side income"; (4) The government draws taxes from the people because it wants to do things for the people. Sichuan Province's taxes have been collected until the 60th year of the Republic of China. In the year 22 of the Republic of China, the government certainly cannot and has no way to do things for the people in the era of the 60th year of the Republic of China, so it simply says: This over-collected tax is the "side income" of the Sichuan Provincial Government. Other examples include the intellectuals of Beiping and Tianjin "knowing" that North China is very dangerous, advocating that cultural relics should be transported south, schools should be moved south, and lives should be escaped to the south... This clever "knowing" is the "side income" in terms of knowledge. As for the gentlemen who usually do extremely bad things, they eat vegetarian food, chant scriptures, and set up Taoist altars,

Hoping that there will be no bad retribution in the future, this is even more trying to "find side income"!

However, some "side income" is extremely unfortunate! For example: the 30 million compatriots in the Northeast are clearly and truly Chinese, but now they are unexpectedly forced to be "Manchurians" under the Japanese iron hoofs: the people of Sichuan pay taxes until the 60th year of the Republic of China, but they have to escape two or three times a year to escape military disasters, and even be wronged ghosts under artillery fire two or three times. This unfortunate and undue harvest is an extremely painful "side income"!

Alas! Chinese people, whether happy or unhappy, are competing to live on "side income," or desperately trying to "find side income," which is why China is what it is today!

The Secrets of Hotels 23

— Yu Xian

Hotels are the so-called business platforms of the past, which are used to facilitate travelers, and there seems to be no secret between them: But our so-called Oriental Paris hotels are the opposite: large hotels with five or six floors are increasing year by year, the decoration strives to be beautiful, and the style strives to be modern, so the travelers are not authentic goods, but become playing with women: the secrets of hotels also arise from this.

Yesterday, because I was sending a friend to Chongqing, I, the country bumpkin, also stepped into the hotel for flirting with women. A room as big as my small building sells for seven silver dollars a day. Who says China is poor? It's really like sitting in a well and looking at the sky. Aren't Shanghai's hotels hanging up signs every day that they are full?

In a moment, a burst of high-heeled leather shoes came from the corridor, and at the same time a colorful piece of paper flew in from the door crack. After all, I, the country bumpkin, is still a country bumpkin, so I quickly grabbed it to look at it. It turned out to be an advertisement for a female fortune teller, which said:

XX has learned a lot in the way of physiognomy. All circles resisting to death vow

Gentlemen, those who want to ask about financial fortune, fleeting years, future prospects, whether by invitation or by telephone notification, will be served immediately. ｜In addition to talking about physiognomy, all socializing is declined｜

XX, as a weak woman, is driven by social trends and has to learn a skill to save herself in life; if legal scholars give guidance, she will be overwhelmed with welcome, or if she is introduced to talk about physiognomy, she will especially look forward to it. The fee for physiognomy is only two yuan, and she respectfully declines any inappropriate gifts. She hereby announces that she has illuminated the situation.

Using physiognomy skills as XX's exclusive business 保重personality and reputation as XX's only purpose

Gentlemen, if you don't talk about physiognomy, please don't invite her, especially solemnly stated again.

Secrets to Getting Ahead in the World 24

— Zi Wei

Flatter whenever there's an opportunity

Brag loudly when the time is right

###

They reside at Room XXX, XX Hotel, Racecourse. Furthermore, a portrait of beautiful, alluring eyes is printed right in the center, as if telling people to recognize the trademark to avoid mistakes.

I couldn't help but recall the aftermath of the Yang Wenying murder case reported yesterday, wasn't it related to this "cherishing personality and reputation" X X? I shall refrain from elaborating due to the vulgar language involved. Perhaps readers haven't forgotten the Chen Xinzhai animalistic affair from last year, as a similar incident is present in this murder case as well.

I won't delve into whether the facts are true, but at the very least, I have many doubts regarding this colored advertisement:

(1) Every day, I flip through newspapers and walk the streets, yet I never see this kind of fortune-telling advertisement, but instead, it's distributed to various hotels by young women.

(2) Is printing one's own portrait akin to asking fortune-tellers to evaluate the quality of a product? Although I've seen the portrait of True Leftist in newspapers because he uses his left-handed calligraphy as a selling point, are their eyes, seeming to hold back tears, also a skill for fortune-telling?

(3) The phrases "Apart from fortune-telling, all social engagements are declined" and "Respectfully refuse inappropriate gifts" have set a new record for advertisements. I've never seen someone building a house ask a doctor to tell fortunes, and fortune-telling is fortune-telling, so why specifically state "Decline all social engagements"? As for "Respectfully refuse inappropriate gifts," I don't know what prompted such a statement.

(4) Their main base is located in XX Hotel. I cannot assert that using a hotel as a fortune-telling place is immoral, but hotels in Shanghai are generally recognized as secret locations. How can a fortune-teller who charges only two yuan for a reading afford to operate in a high-end hotel frequented by young masters seeking pleasure and fortune? How do they "make a living to save themselves"?

Later, advertisements for XXX Massage Parlor continued to fly in through the door crack. Shanghai is, after all, Shanghai; it constantly produces new and exciting things. I hope that in the near future, perhaps tomorrow, all buildings in Shanghai will be converted into hotels. When the Japanese invade the Yangtze River region, let them experience the variety of Shanghai's mirror tricks. I guarantee they'll find so much pleasure here that they'll forget about home and stop their northward advance to instead attack southern Guangdong.

Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde 25

— Gan

Since the Japanese troops invaded Rehe, bombed the Great Wall, and shocked Tianjin and Beijing, people and experts have unanimously said that the military strength is too disparate and the nation cannot resist. In reality, while the Japanese troops' weapons are indeed formidable, deep down everyone had long arranged for the enemy's smooth advance, coupled with a few staged retreats, a tacit understanding between the two sides.

Things can indeed be insured. Currently, it seems that besides opium-addicted generals, there are not many who openly emulate Li Hongzhang, although many still secretly harbor such intentions. They wouldn't go so far as to stick out their tongues and shout, "Master, please come in." However, China has a wealth of talent, and the writers and scholars who don't want the talents of Jiang and Han to take all the glory feel the love (sic?) for their country and dare not lag behind. Although they dare not openly poison wells and kill four hundred million compatriots, they can certainly hide behind and stab a few times, echoing the Japanese troops. The only worry is that the hearts of the Chinese people are not dead, which would be terrible.

Recently, in the old lands of Yan and Zhao, a famous cultural city, there is a strange phenomenon. This person is neither a god nor a spirit, but a demon-like figure, born from the descendants of the Jin and Yuan dynasties, pretending to be Chinese, wielding his eloquent pen to write an obituary for the national crisis. He first advocated knocking on the doors of the League of Nations to seek joint governance, but the detestable Japanese devils were too ignorant and insisted on sole occupation. So he hatched a plan, transformed himself, put on Han Chinese attire, and looked like a Japanese doctor. Then, he turned his brush around and shouted: "We have been forced onto Mount Liang" (note, not the doctor going to Mount Liang). Reading further, it seems he's at least going to put on a bloody war of resistance. No, readers, rest assured, the doctor will never take you to the front lines. On the contrary, thinking from the "conscience" of the Japanese, truly "we cannot go against our conscience and advocate a declaration of war against Japan." And in order to "be fair to the United States and the League of Nations," the fundamental strategy is naturally to "persist in moral non-recognition." The implied opposite is that there's no need to fight back, just endure a few more blows. If the Japanese troops stubbornly refuse to stop, then we can only sacrifice with pain, because "we can wait fifty years." Of course, there's no need to say any more, the grand plan to save the nation and the wonderful writing techniques are all in this.

Enough, enough! The doctor is working so hard, even if he's not entirely genuine, at least his heart and soul have been Japanized. If my words are not wrong, when the empire's great undertaking is completed, the common people who resist Japan will not be spared. But the doctor can guarantee high official positions and generous rewards. If the doctor lives to a ripe old age, and fifty years later, China's national destiny flourishes, then he can return wearing wooden clogs and watch the peace, which would be truly delightful. If, unfortunately, this person passes away early, the Chinese people, in remembrance, might have the blessing of a crystal coffin to enjoy.

However, what the doctor did not expect is that imperialist oppression and enslavement have already laid the groundwork for the Chinese national revolutionary war, and Japan is igniting a fire on the fuse. At this time, a great power will erupt, and perhaps the "fifty years" of hope will be greatly discounted.

So, what will the doctor do? Only another transformation… right?

A Prominent Figure's Diary (Imagined) 26

— Bing

X Month X Day

Woke up at eleven o'clock. Before washing up, the secretary reported on current affairs, noting subtle changes in the political situation. Immediately telephoned the editor-in-chief of the X newspaper, informed them of the confidential matters, instructed them to relay the information to all comrades, and scheduled a meeting at the X Hotel at 3 PM.

Ate raw milk and a tonic containing three eggs, a small amount. Went out to visit Comrade X to discuss strategies for dealing with the political coup. He advocated acting alone, but I believed that under certain circumstances, we should closely coordinate with various opposition factions. The ancients taught that "many hands make light work," and besides, the X faction has deep roots and cannot be overthrown by one faction alone. He smiled and nodded in agreement. Afterwards, we briefly discussed trivial matters related to women. He praised the X dance hall star Xiao Qiu, saying that she was willing to do as I wished; however, I still needed to give it some thought.

Left and went to X Restaurant for lunch, spending eight silver dollars. It was already four o'clock when I rushed to the X Hotel. The comrades had already arrived. At the meeting, three important resolutions were passed: first, to contact various opposition factions; second, to issue a declaration regarding the coup; and third, to intensify propaganda against X.

Returned to my residence and found eight name cards on the table. Except for the special representative of the X faction X, the rest were all comrades. Went out in the evening with Comrades X, X, and X.

Page 21

Active in various places. Etc. Rejected.

Left the dance hall. Curfew in effect. Checked into the hotel to prevent accidents. Telephoned the residence secretary with confidential instructions.

X Month X Day

Around ten o'clock, Minister X and Commissioner X came, eagerly urging me to take the position of X. I had originally declined because I thought the area was undeveloped, but my subordinates were extremely eager, frequently inquiring. Now that the situation is inflexible, I will temporarily comply.

After breakfast, a group of reporters arrived. I made a statement, saying, "Urged by various parties, I have decided to take the position of X today. I will hold the swearing-in ceremony later."

In the afternoon, I went to the X Bureau with the secretary and seven others. After resting briefly, the secretary distributed the press release to the reporters, revealing the new list of department members. The old staff jointly submitted their resignations, which were approved. X was a lifelong friend and was newly appointed. The others received the endorsement: "Will be introduced to a new position."

I inspected the bureau once, opened the bureau treasury, and found three thousand silver dollars, which I took back with me.

Returned to my residence, where the courtyard was like a marketplace, filled with old acquaintances, whom I told, "Will be appointed later," and they dispersed.

In the evening, I telegraphed my relatives, asking them again about the types of positions they would like to take. The position of Director of Finance was the most sought after.

Went to the X Dance Hall with the dance star and went to X Company for shopping, spending one thousand six hundred silver dollars. The dance star sent the items back by car, while I went to the X Hotel. After waiting for a long time for the dance star to arrive, I couldn't restrain myself and called a girl to relieve my boredom. Before I even undressed, dawn had broken. I fell asleep with her in a daze. Suddenly, I remembered that I had banquets at three locations, including X, and that X and others had meetings. I got out of bed and called the residence secretary to quickly relay the message that all engagements were canceled.

X Month X Day

In the morning, Minister X came and prepared to refute the various rumors. X still hopes I will stay, urging me not to lose heart. However, I had already drafted my telegram of resignation and was determined. I went inside and told the secretary to send the telegram as planned.

After a small tonic and breakfast, I took my family by car to the train station and boarded the express train, arriving in X Port at 3 PM. A large number of telegrams had been sent to the residence, all urging me not to lose heart, because they suspected that I had already come to X Port, so they telegraphed directly here.

Having just unpacked, I was extremely tired. A group of reporters arrived at my heels, and I made a statement, saying, "I am suffering from a relapse of an old illness and cannot bear the burden of the X position, so I have repeatedly insisted on resigning and have come to the port to rest and recuperate. Now my wish has been granted. As for the plan to resist foreign aggression and save the country, we should act with sincerity, eliminate selfish views, and work together to overcome the national crisis."

Around four o'clock, to avoid the noise, I moved to the X Hospital and refused to see visitors, instructing them to properly resolve the situation.

In the evening, I and Xiao Qiu went to the X Hospital… and suddenly felt cheerful.

After leaving the theater, I went to X Company to buy decorations and returned to the hospital fully loaded. Foreign aid goods cost three hundred silver dollars, and I consumed them immediately upon arrival at the hospital.

One after another, I summoned the secretary and eight staff members, instructing them on the countermeasures.

My wife stayed in the hospital, and we talked in detail until dawn.

Abolish Prostitution Prohibition 27

— Youngster

It is said that the degree of development of urban civilization is measured by the number of brothels, the prosperity of gambling dens, and the drama of kidnapping cases and behind-the-scenes dealings. Moreover, they are directly proportional. Shanghai has become the greatest metropolis in our country precisely because it fits this formula. In other words (friends, please don't scold me for being arbitrary, blindly following, or absurdly inappropriate): if you want a place to become a lively and civilized city, there is only one way, absolutely only this one way, to equip it with the basic conditions that a city should have and make them complete, widespread, and universal. Then, it will naturally not let Shanghai have all the glory, and may even surpass Shanghai, you never know!

Nanjing is our expensive and large capital of the Republic of China, the Central Party Headquarters is located there, the Central Government is located there, the Central University is also located there, and foreigners, foreign envoys, and foreign goods enter and flood the city, so it has been listed as one of the six major cities in the country. However, although Nanjing is called a city, it has always lacked the basic conditions that a metropolis should have. (Someone said definitively that Nanjing is not as lively as Shanghai because of this major reason.) Just talking about brothels, they suffer from the "prohibition" order and cannot grow freely, which hurts the fact that adults and gentlemen have nowhere to vent their sexual desires, and they desperately run to Shanghai. Delaying some unimportant official business is not a big deal, but traveling back and forth in the wind and dust may harm their health, so this is not a long-term solution! This Youngster is deeply worried about this!

Good news! The bill to abolish prostitution prohibition has actually passed! This Youngster reverently read the special telegram three and a half times, washed his hands and put them together, and sincerely shouted from the depths of his soul, "The savior has come, Amitabha! Well done, well done, this is the blessing of my Buddha Bodhisattva manifesting!" From now on, the "beings of Nanjing" will be saved! However, strangely! Why did the female representatives not understand the greater good and cry bitterly in resistance? Are the female representatives' tears so easily shed and worthless? Only heaven knows!

A fragment of her life

Two or three years passed, and Miss Liu grew even more beautiful.

She learned many Kunqu operas, and she also played the sanxian very well. No teacher who taught her singing didn't praise her for being capable. Later, Peking opera gradually became popular in the brothel, so she had to learn "Qin Qiong Selling His Horse" or "Su San Being Escorted," as well as master the "Xipi" and "Erhuang" styles.

From this, it can be seen that being human is not easy, and even being a prostitute is so difficult.

Movie Magazine

A Singer's Luck in Hollywood 29

— Zhong Qin

Bing Crosby pioneered the trend

Major stars have to practice singing

From the beginning when silent films were abandoned and sound films became popular, the film industry realized the importance of music and the necessity of singing in sound films. But at first, there wasn't the current intense need for RADIO STAR singers. Recently, we will never forget Bing Crosby, who as a singer was the first to occupy a position in the film world, with everyone admiring his singing voice. After Bing Crosby's rise, Hollywood film companies all spent huge sums of money to recruit singers from the music industry. Thus, in recent times, singers have had the luckiest period in Hollywood, which is an inevitable trend since the discovery of sound films.

Bing Crosby only has a three-year history in Hollywood. When he first arrived in Hollywood, his first song was a segment from a song. Because his voice was famous in the American music scene, his first performance received praise from many critics as a voice that "lingered for three days". This song was inserted into the Paramount production "The Big Broadcast", and Bing Crosby was officially hired as an actor by Paramount.

Following Bing Crosby, the singer was Kate Smith. When she performed at the Broadway Music Association, although she often didn't have time to go on stage until late at night, her fans never left until dawn. The magic of her singing was also amazing. Paramount, admiring her reputation, paid a large sum of money to bring her into the film industry. After joining Paramount, she only made one film, "Hello Everybody", and became a movie star like Bing Crosby, because she was a singer. Paramount Company was the first to hire singers to be actors in Hollywood.

Paramount's two singers were highly praised by critics, so Fox, RKO, Warner Brothers, Columbia and other major companies also successively hired well-known singers from the Broadway music scene. At the same time, the status of movie stars who were also singers suddenly rose. At this time, film industry figures all competed to practice their voices in order to maintain their position in the film world. Even Greta Garbo and John Gilbert had to practice singing, and it almost became a trend that anyone who couldn't sing was not worthy of being a film industry figure.

More recently, the trend of Hollywood worshiping singers has reached its peak. Since January of this year, about twenty singers have entered the film industry in Hollywood, and their salaries are higher than those of ordinary movie stars. Therefore, Mr. Big Nose Jimmy Durante also often went to the music academy to practice singing. Although it seems ridiculous, the general trend can be seen.

Film Review

Review of "A Woman Commands" 30

— Ming

The story and direction are ordinary

But the rest is mostly commendable

Pola Negri doesn't have many sound films, and her reputation is far less than it was four or five years ago when she was popular. I saw her in "A Woman Commands", which was shown at the New Light Theater yesterday, and she looked much older. She plays a singer who is in love with a young military officer, and the young military officer, in order to please the singer, not only goes bankrupt but also incurs huge debts. So she took out her own ornaments to pay off his debts for him and left him to resume her singing career. Soon, the king traveled incognito and, at first sight, greatly admired her, inviting her to the palace for a banquet. Soon after, he made her queen. But the soldiers and civilians of the country, long resentful of the king's tyranny, rose up in revolution. The king died, and she, as queen, was also sentenced to death. However, the young military officer devised a plan to intercede, and they left the country together.

Her entire performance was excellent, and the inner expressions in several close-ups were quite moving. The conflict between emotion and reason was revealed in the two scenes of painful parting and taking the position of queen. The king's ambiguous attitude, like love but not love, was just right. The two songs she sang were very tragic. The same song was sung over and over again, but the environment and attitude changed, so even the tones were different, and it wasn't repetitive. Indeed, not only in this film is she the chief, but few Hollywood actresses can match her, right?

Basil Rathbone, who played the young military officer, is a very ordinary playboy with few facial expressions. However, in fact, he is still qualified in the entire film. Roland Young, who played the emperor, was truly wonderful. He portrayed a lecherous and dim-witted king thoroughly... Hollywood's comedic stars

Wheeler and Woolsey 31

— Jie Ke

Arriving in Shanghai this afternoon

Wheeler and Woolsey, a famous comedic star duo from RKO Pictures, will arrive in Shanghai this afternoon (Saturday) by ship. They are currently traveling around the world on vacation and will stay in Shanghai for a week. The Shanghai branch of RKO is preparing to give them a grand welcome upon their arrival. During their week-long tour of the Paris of the East, they are prepared to do their utmost to entertain them. RKO's Shanghai branch has already organized a welcome committee, headed by the company's general manager Knight and the general manager of Nanyiyi Company, He Tingran, among others. When they arrive at the pier, Chinese music will be played along with a Western music band, and many firecrackers will be set off to add to the excitement. Madie Motor Company has also prepared a Packard car for them to use when touring Shanghai. The films Wheeler and Woolsey have starred in include "Peach O'Reno", "Caught Plastered", "Girl Crazy", and the unreleased "Hold 'Em Jail" and "Diplomaniacs", which Shanghai movie audiences should not have forgotten.

, although there are excesses, it is thorough and makes people applaud. Two supporting roles, one the singer's maid and the other the Minister of the Interior, also performed the essence of humor, making people laugh non-stop with every word and action.

There are many beautiful shots, the most wonderful being the singer looking out at the street scene from the window, a scene of ice and snow, which is more beautiful than any picture. The sets are also quite grand. The scene changes are very compact, and although there are many dialogues, they are very interesting and the pronunciation is clear.

The entire play does not reveal the historical background. If it is said to be a historical drama, the costumes, sets, and dialogues are mostly modern. If it is a new script, then why do so many customs and habits seem to be from a time before today? It is truly somewhat illogical. Moreover, the attitude of the ministers toward the king is too outrageous. The screenwriter seems to have lost control.

Fortunately, the actors were all very good, otherwise, this film would have been very mediocre and dull.

Review of "The Property Man" 32

— Ling He

A patchwork of old fragments,

Yet surprisingly sells out.

A while ago, I saw "A Streetcar Named Desire" once. Not long ago, the Nanjing Grand Theater showed "The Policeman," both of which were Charlie Chaplin's past works. Given the audience's great desire for the works of this "King of Comedy," they naturally flocked to see them, drawn by the prominent advertisements in the newspapers. Similarly, under such circumstances, "The Property Man" emerged in response to the demand.

The so-called "Property Man" is pieced together from many old films of Chaplin's from over a decade ago. Naturally, it lacks a coherent plot. Although the opportunistic film merchant put in great effort to connect the pieces back and forth, trying to convince the audience that this is "one" film, there is no consistent story in it.

The content is roughly as follows: Chaplin first works as a bartender in a bar, causing a ruckus. He suddenly meets a noble woman, attends a banquet, and causes another ruckus. Later, he participates in a car race, sporting not only his signature mustache but also two strands of hair on his chin. Then, somehow, he becomes a stage property man, naturally getting into several fights and tumbling around. (At this point, the chin hairs suddenly disappear.) Finally, he becomes a referee for a boxing match, still causing a great commotion.

Since the plot is as described above, Charlie Chaplin lacks a consistent character portrayal from beginning to end, so there is nothing to critique.

Being an old film from over a decade ago, the screening is naturally rough and the dubbing is extremely childish.

In short, this film is a prank by an opportunistic film merchant. However, yesterday it was almost a sold-out show in Paris, showing how unexpectedly appealing Chaplin still is.

Film Novel: 42nd Street (7) 33

— Siping

Dillon's car arrived. He got out of the car, helping Enloewell out, and announced to everyone that this was the future star. Everyone was very disappointed to hear this. They all knew that En was not capable of replacing Dorsay. Dillon, because En was even more flattering than Dorsay, tried his best to persuade Mashie, guaranteeing that she could become a big star. After hearing Dillon's compliments, En opened her mouth and said, "To be honest, I am not qualified enough. But I know there is someone in this group who is very suitable. Mr. Mashie, as long as you can try her."

"Who is that?" Mashie asked.

"Pansy Shadyou," En said. "Marsh said," Mr. Mashie, listen. I have been waiting for such an opportunity for many years. If I didn't believe she was the best, how could I miss the opportunity myself?"

"Ask her to come in," Mashie said immediately without thinking.

Since the "Beautiful Women" dance performance had Pansy as the star, it opened on that evening at the time announced in the advertisement. Everyone felt nervous that day, and Pansy's heart was beating especially fast: she felt so nervous that she seemed to lose her emotions. But that night…

That night, even people who don't usually go to the theater were sure to see the scene where Pansy fell into Pylai's arms, which was not like watching a play at all, but like watching a real love affair. The love song in that scene was TINPANALLEY, but Pylai sang this love song in a soft and charming tone, unmatched by any musical comedy.

That night, Pansy was doubly happy because, before the curtain rose, Dorsay hobbled into her dressing room.

"When I came here tonight," Dorsay said, "I originally wanted to pull out all your hair. Then I changed my mind. I think I have fulfilled my wish, and now it's your chance. You like fame, maybe you can become famous. As for me, I love Pant. We can get married tomorrow."

After the curtain call, Pylai went to Pansy's dressing room.

"Listen, honey," he said to Pansy, "I was just about to tell you, I..."

"Please say it," Pansy urged.

"I think this is a bit funny," Pylai stammered, unable to say it. "Doesn't this already make you understand?"

Pylai pulled her into his arms, then lifted her face towards him, and his lips slowly approached hers. This must not be a stage kiss (The End)
